<s> bungay nodded his head in a knowing manner and winked his eyes when the captain came to the waterloo passage and warrington burst out laughing <\s>
<s> you see how our venerable friend bungay is affected shandon said slily looking up from his papers that's your true sort of test <\s>
<s> i have used the duke of wellington and the battle of waterloo a hundred times and i never knew the duke to fail <\s>
<s> the captain then went on to confess with much candour that up to the present time the gentlemen of england confident of their right and careless of those who questioned it had left the political interest of their order as they did the management of their estates or the settlement of their legal affairs to persons affected to each peculiar service and had permitted their interests to be represented in the press by professional proctors and advocates <\s>
<s> that time shandon professed to consider was now gone by the gentlemen of england must be their own champions the declared enemies of their order were brave strong numerous and uncompromising <\s>
<s> they must meet their foes in the field they must not be belied and misrepresented by hireling advocates they must not have grub street publishing gazettes from whitehall that's a dig at bacon's people mr <\s>
<s> bungay said shandon turning round to the publisher <\s>
<s> bungay clapped his stick on the floor <\s>
<s> hang him pitch into him capting he said with exultation and turning to warrington wagged his dull head more vehemently than ever and said for a slashing article sir there's nobody like the capting no obody like him <\s>
<s> the prospectus writer went on to say that some gentlemen whose names were for obvious reasons not brought before the public at which mr <\s>
<s> warrington began to laugh again had determined to bring forward a journal of which the principles were so and so <\s>
<s> these men are proud of their order and anxious to uphold it cried out captain shandon flourishing his paper with a grin <\s>
<s> they are loyal to their sovereign by faithful conviction and ancestral allegiance they love their church where they would have their children worship and for which their forefathers bled they love their country and would keep it what the gentlemen of england yes the gentlemen of england we'll have that in large caps bungay my boy have made it the greatest and freest in the world and as the names of some of them are appended to the deed which secured our liberties at runnymede what's that <\s>
<s> an ancestor of mine sealed it with his sword hilt pen said with great gravity <\s>
<s> it's the habeas corpus mr <\s>
<s> bungay warrington said on which the publisher answered all right i dare say and yawned though he said go on capting <\s>
<s> at runnymede they are ready to defend that freedom to day with sword and pen and now as then to rally round the old laws and liberties of england <\s>
<s> the little child stood wondering the lady was working silently and looking with fond admiration <\s>
<s> come here little mary said warrington and patted the child's fair curls with his large hand <\s>
<s> but she shrank back from his rough caress and preferred to go and take refuge at pen's knee and play with his fine watch chain and pen was very much pleased that she came to him for he was very soft hearted and simple though he concealed his gentleness under a shy and pompous demeanour <\s>
<s> so she clambered up on his lap whilst her father continued to read his programme <\s>
<s> you were laughing the captain said to warrington about the obvious reasons which i mentioned <\s>
<s> now i'll show ye what they are ye unbelieving heathen <\s>
<s> we have said he went on that we cannot give the names of the parties engaged in this undertaking and that there were obvious reasons for that concealment <\s>
<s> we number influential friends in both houses of the senate and have secured allies in every diplomatic circle in europe <\s>
<s> our sources of intelligence are such as cannot by any possibility be made public and indeed such as no other london or european journal could by any chance acquire <\s>
<s> but this we are free to say that the very earliest information connected with the movement of english and continental politics will be found only in the columns of the pall mall gazette the statesman and the capitalist the country gentleman and the divine will be amongst our readers because our writers are amongst them <\s>
<s> we address ourselves to the higher circles of society we care not to disown it the pall mall gazette is written by gentlemen for gentlemen its conductors speak to the classes in which they live and were born <\s>
<s> the field preacher has his journal the radical free thinker has his journal why should the gentlemen of england be unrepresented in the press mr <\s>
<s> shandon then went on with much modesty to descant upon the literary and fashionable departments of the pall mall gazette which were to be conducted by gentlemen of acknowledged reputation men famous at the universities at which mr pendennis could scarcely help laughing and blushing known at the clubs and of the society which they described <\s>
<s> he pointed out delicately to advertisers that there would be no such medium as the pall mall gazette for giving publicity to their sales and he eloquently called upon the nobility of england the baronetage of england the revered clergy of england the bar of england the matrons the daughters the homes and hearths of england to rally round the good old cause and bungay at the conclusion of the reading woke up from a second snooze in which he had indulged himself and again said it was all right <\s>
<s> the reading of the prospectus concluded the gentlemen present entered into some details regarding the political and literary management of the paper and mr <\s>
<s> bungay sate by listening and nodding his head as if he understood what was the subject of their conversation and approved of their opinions <\s>
<s> bungay's opinions in truth were pretty simple <\s>
<s> he thought the captain could write the best smashing article in england <\s>
<s> he wanted the opposition house of bacon smashed and it was his opinion that the captain could do that business <\s>
<s> if the captain had written a letter of junius on a sheet of paper or copied a part of the church catechism mr <\s>
<s> bungay would have been perfectly contented and have considered that the article was a smashing article <\s>
<s> and he pocketed the papers with the greatest satisfaction and he not only paid for the ms as we have seen but he called little mary to him and gave her a penny as he went away <\s>
<s> the reading of the manuscript over the party engaged in general conversation shandon leading with a jaunty fashionable air in compliment to the two guests who sate with him and and who by their appearance and manner he presumed to be persons of the beau monde <\s>
<s> he knew very little indeed of the great world but he had seen it and made the most of what he had seen <\s>
<s> he spoke of the characters of the day and great personages of the fashion with easy familiarity and jocular allusions as if it had been his habit to live amongst them <\s>
<s> he told anecdotes of their private life and of conversations he had had and entertainments at which he had been present and at which such and such a thing occurred <\s>
<s> pen was amused to hear the shabby prisoner in a tattered dressing gown talking glibly about the great of the land <\s>
<s> shandon was always delighted when her husband told these tales and believed in them fondly every one <\s>
<s> she did not want to mingle in the fashionable world herself she was not clever enough but the great society was the very place for her charles he shone in it he was respected in it <\s>
<s> indeed shandon had once been asked to dinner by the earl of x his wife treasured the invitation card in her workbox at that very day <\s>
<s> bungay presently had enough of this talk and got up to take leave whereupon warrington and pen rose to depart with the publisher though the latter would have liked to stay to make a further acquaintance with this family who interested him and touched him <\s>
<s> he said something about hoping for permission to repeat his visit upon which shandon with a rueful grin said he was always to be found at home and should be delighted to see mr <\s>
<s> i'll see you to my park gate gentlemen said captain shandon seizing his hat in spite of a deprecatory look and a faint cry of charles from mrs <\s>
<s> and the captain in shabby slippers shuffled out before his guests leading the way through the dismal passages of the prison <\s>
<s> his hand was already fiddling with his waistcoat pocket where bungay's five pound note was as he took leave of the three gentlemen at the wicket one of them mr <\s>
<s> arthur pendennis being greatly relieved when he was out of the horrid place and again freely treading the flags of farringdon street <\s>
<s> shandon sadly went on with her work at the window looking into the court <\s>
<s> she saw shandon with a couple of men at his heels run rapidly in the direction of the prison tavern <\s>
<s> she had hoped to have had him to dinner herself that day there was a piece of meat and some salad in a basin on the ledge outside of the window of their room which she had expected that she and little mary were to share with the child's father <\s>
<s> but there was no chance of that now <\s>
<s> he would be in that tavern until the hours for closing it then he would go and play at cards or drink in some other man's room and come back silent with glazed eyes reeling a little on his walk that his wife might nurse him <\s>
<s> oh what varieties of pain do we not make our women suffer <\s>
<s> shandon went to the cupboard and in lieu of a dinner made herself some tea <\s>
<s> and in those varieties of pain of which we spoke anon what a part of confidante has that poor tea pot played ever since the kindly plant was introduced among us <\s>
<s> what myriads of women have cried over it to be sure <\s>
<s> what sick beds it has smoked by <\s>
<s> what fevered lips have received refreshment from out of it <\s>

<s> jack finucane a townsman of captain shandon's found the captain's wife and little mary for whom jack always brought a sweetmeat in his pocket over this meal <\s>
<s> jack thought shandon the greatest of created geniuses had had one or two helps from the good natured prodigal who had always a kind word and sometimes a guinea for any friend in need and never missed a day in seeing his patron <\s>
<s> he was ready to run shandon's errands and transact his money business with publishers and newspaper editors duns creditors holders of shandon's acceptances gentlemen disposed to speculate in those securities and to transact the thousand little affairs of an embarrassed irish gentleman <\s>
<s> i never knew an embarrassed irish gentleman yet but he had an aide de camp of his own nation likewise in circumstances of pecuniary discomfort <\s>

<s> the publisher and the two gentlemen had had some talk together after quitting shandon and warrington reiterated to bungay what he had said to his rival bacon viz that pen was a high fellow of great genius and what was more well with the great world and related to no end of the peerage <\s>

<s> hang him pitch into him capting he said with exultation and turning to warrington wagged his dull head more vehemently than ever and said for a slashing article sir there's nobody like the capting no obody like him <\s>
<s> the prospectus writer went on to say that some gentlemen whose names were for obvious reasons not brought before the public at which mr <\s>
<s> warrington began to laugh again had determined to bring forward a journal of which the principles were so and so <\s>
<s> these men are proud of their order and anxious to uphold it cried out captain shandon flourishing his paper with a grin <\s>
<s> they are loyal to their sovereign by faithful conviction and ancestral allegiance they love their church where they would have their children worship and for which their forefathers bled they love their country and would keep it what the gentlemen of england yes the gentlemen of england we'll have that in large caps bungay my boy have made it the greatest and freest in the world and as the names of some of them are appended to the deed which secured our liberties at runnymede what's that <\s>
<s> an ancestor of mine sealed it with his sword hilt pen said with great gravity <\s>
<s> it's the habeas corpus mr <\s>
<s> bungay warrington said on which the publisher answered all right i dare say and yawned though he said go on capting <\s>
<s> at runnymede they are ready to defend that freedom to day with sword and pen and now as then to rally round the old laws and liberties of england <\s>
<s> the little child stood wondering the lady was working silently and looking with fond admiration <\s>
<s> come here little mary said warrington and patted the child's fair curls with his large hand <\s>
<s> but she shrank back from his rough caress and preferred to go and take refuge at pen's knee and play with his fine watch chain and pen was very much pleased that she came to him for he was very soft hearted and simple though he concealed his gentleness under a shy and pompous demeanour <\s>
<s> so she clambered up on his lap whilst her father continued to read his programme <\s>
<s> you were laughing the captain said to warrington about the obvious reasons which i mentioned <\s>
<s> now i'll show ye what they are ye unbelieving heathen <\s>
<s> we have said he went on that we cannot give the names of the parties engaged in this undertaking and that there were obvious reasons for that concealment <\s>
<s> we number influential friends in both houses of the senate and have secured allies in every diplomatic circle in europe <\s>
<s> our sources of intelligence are such as cannot by any possibility be made public and indeed such as no other london or european journal could by any chance acquire <\s>
<s> but this we are free to say that the very earliest information connected with the movement of english and continental politics will be found only in the columns of the pall mall gazette the statesman and the capitalist the country gentleman and the divine will be amongst our readers because our writers are amongst them <\s>
<s> we address ourselves to the higher circles of society we care not to disown it the pall mall gazette is written by gentlemen for gentlemen its conductors speak to the classes in which they live and were born <\s>
<s> the field preacher has his journal the radical free thinker has his journal why should the gentlemen of england be unrepresented in the press mr <\s>
<s> shandon then went on with much modesty to descant upon the literary and fashionable departments of the pall mall gazette which were to be conducted by gentlemen of acknowledged reputation men famous at the universities at which mr pendennis could scarcely help laughing and blushing known at the clubs and of the society which they described <\s>
<s> he pointed out delicately to advertisers that there would be no such medium as the pall mall gazette for giving publicity to their sales and he eloquently called upon the nobility of england the baronetage of england the revered clergy of england the bar of england the matrons the daughters the homes and hearths of england to rally round the good old cause and bungay at the conclusion of the reading woke up from a second snooze in which he had indulged himself and again said it was all right <\s>
<s> the reading of the prospectus concluded the gentlemen present entered into some details regarding the political and literary management of the paper and mr <\s>
<s> bungay sate by listening and nodding his head as if he understood what was the subject of their conversation and approved of their opinions <\s>
<s> bungay's opinions in truth were pretty simple <\s>
<s> he thought the captain could write the best smashing article in england <\s>
<s> he wanted the opposition house of bacon smashed and it was his opinion that the captain could do that business <\s>
<s> if the captain had written a letter of junius on a sheet of paper or copied a part of the church catechism mr <\s>
<s> bungay would have been perfectly contented and have considered that the article was a smashing article <\s>
<s> and he pocketed the papers with the greatest satisfaction and he not only paid for the ms as we have seen but he called little mary to him and gave her a penny as he went away <\s>
<s> the reading of the manuscript over the party engaged in general conversation shandon leading with a jaunty fashionable air in compliment to the two guests who sate with him and and who by their appearance and manner he presumed to be persons of the beau monde <\s>
<s> he knew very little indeed of the great world but he had seen it and made the most of what he had seen <\s>
<s> he spoke of the characters of the day and great personages of the fashion with easy familiarity and jocular allusions as if it had been his habit to live amongst them <\s>
<s> he told anecdotes of their private life and of conversations he had had and entertainments at which he had been present and at which such and such a thing occurred <\s>
<s> pen was amused to hear the shabby prisoner in a tattered dressing gown talking glibly about the great of the land <\s>
<s> shandon was always delighted when her husband told these tales and believed in them fondly every one <\s>
<s> she did not want to mingle in the fashionable world herself she was not clever enough but the great society was the very place for her charles he shone in it he was respected in it <\s>
<s> indeed shandon had once been asked to dinner by the earl of x his wife treasured the invitation card in her workbox at that very day <\s>
<s> bungay presently had enough of this talk and got up to take leave whereupon warrington and pen rose to depart with the publisher though the latter would have liked to stay to make a further acquaintance with this family who interested him and touched him <\s>
<s> he said something about hoping for permission to repeat his visit upon which shandon with a rueful grin said he was always to be found at home and should be delighted to see mr <\s>
<s> i'll see you to my park gate gentlemen said captain shandon seizing his hat in spite of a deprecatory look and a faint cry of charles from mrs <\s>
<s> and the captain in shabby slippers shuffled out before his guests leading the way through the dismal passages of the prison <\s>
<s> his hand was already fiddling with his waistcoat pocket where bungay's five pound note was as he took leave of the three gentlemen at the wicket one of them mr <\s>
<s> arthur pendennis being greatly relieved when he was out of the horrid place and again freely treading the flags of farringdon street <\s>
<s> shandon sadly went on with her work at the window looking into the court <\s>
<s> she saw shandon with a couple of men at his heels run rapidly in the direction of the prison tavern <\s>
<s> she had hoped to have had him to dinner herself that day there was a piece of meat and some salad in a basin on the ledge outside of the window of their room which she had expected that she and little mary were to share with the child's father <\s>
<s> but there was no chance of that now <\s>
<s> he would be in that tavern until the hours for closing it then he would go and play at cards or drink in some other man's room and come back silent with glazed eyes reeling a little on his walk that his wife might nurse him <\s>
<s> oh what varieties of pain do we not make our women suffer <\s>
<s> shandon went to the cupboard and in lieu of a dinner made herself some tea <\s>
<s> and in those varieties of pain of which we spoke anon what a part of confidante has that poor tea pot played ever since the kindly plant was introduced among us <\s>
<s> what myriads of women have cried over it to be sure <\s>
<s> what sick beds it has smoked by <\s>
<s> what fevered lips have received refreshment from out of it <\s>
<s> nature meant very gently by women when she made that tea plant and with a little thought what a series of pictures and groups the fancy may conjure up and assemble round the tea pot and cup <\s>
<s> melissa and sacharissa are talking love secrets over it <\s>
<s> poor polly has it and her lover's letters upon the table his letters who was her lover yesterday and when it was with pleasure not despair she wept over them <\s>

<s> shandon and little mary sit down and drink their tea together while the captain goes out and takes his pleasure <\s>
<s> she cares for nothing else but that when her husband is away <\s>
<s> a gentleman with whom we are already slightly acquainted mr <\s>
<s> jack finucane a townsman of captain shandon's found the captain's wife and little mary for whom jack always brought a sweetmeat in his pocket over this meal <\s>
<s> jack thought shandon the greatest of created geniuses had had one or two helps from the good natured prodigal who had always a kind word and sometimes a guinea for any friend in need and never missed a day in seeing his patron <\s>
<s> he was ready to run shandon's errands and transact his money business with publishers and newspaper editors duns creditors holders of shandon's acceptances gentlemen disposed to speculate in those securities and to transact the thousand little affairs of an embarrassed irish gentleman <\s>
<s> i never knew an embarrassed irish gentleman yet but he had an aide de camp of his own nation likewise in circumstances of pecuniary discomfort <\s>
<s> that aide de camp has subordinates of his own who again may have other insolvent dependents all through his life our captain marched at the head of a ragged staff who shared in the rough fortunes of their chieftain <\s>

<s> shandon had given a pound to one follower had sent a leg of mutton and potatoes and beer to an acquaintance in the poor side of the prison had paid an outstanding bill at the tavern where he had changed his five pound note had had a dinner with two friends there to whom he lost sundry half crowns at cards afterwards so that the night left him as poor as the morning had found him <\s>
<s> the publisher and the two gentlemen had had some talk together after quitting shandon and warrington reiterated to bungay what he had said to his rival bacon viz that pen was a high fellow of great genius and what was more well with the great world and related to no end of the peerage <\s>
<s> bungay replied that he should be happy to have dealings with mr <\s>
<s> pendennis and hoped to have the pleasure of seeing both gents to cut mutton with him before long and so with mutual politeness and protestations they parted <\s>

<s> so she clambered up on his lap whilst her father continued to read his programme <\s>
<s> you were laughing the captain said to warrington about the obvious reasons which i mentioned <\s>
<s> now i'll show ye what they are ye unbelieving heathen <\s>
<s> we have said he went on that we cannot give the names of the parties engaged in this undertaking and that there were obvious reasons for that concealment <\s>
<s> we number influential friends in both houses of the senate and have secured allies in every diplomatic circle in europe <\s>
<s> our sources of intelligence are such as cannot by any possibility be made public and indeed such as no other london or european journal could by any chance acquire <\s>
<s> but this we are free to say that the very earliest information connected with the movement of english and continental politics will be found only in the columns of the pall mall gazette the statesman and the capitalist the country gentleman and the divine will be amongst our readers because our writers are amongst them <\s>
<s> we address ourselves to the higher circles of society we care not to disown it the pall mall gazette is written by gentlemen for gentlemen its conductors speak to the classes in which they live and were born <\s>
<s> the field preacher has his journal the radical free thinker has his journal why should the gentlemen of england be unrepresented in the press mr <\s>
<s> shandon then went on with much modesty to descant upon the literary and fashionable departments of the pall mall gazette which were to be conducted by gentlemen of acknowledged reputation men famous at the universities at which mr pendennis could scarcely help laughing and blushing known at the clubs and of the society which they described <\s>
<s> he pointed out delicately to advertisers that there would be no such medium as the pall mall gazette for giving publicity to their sales and he eloquently called upon the nobility of england the baronetage of england the revered clergy of england the bar of england the matrons the daughters the homes and hearths of england to rally round the good old cause and bungay at the conclusion of the reading woke up from a second snooze in which he had indulged himself and again said it was all right <\s>
<s> the reading of the prospectus concluded the gentlemen present entered into some details regarding the political and literary management of the paper and mr <\s>
<s> bungay sate by listening and nodding his head as if he understood what was the subject of their conversation and approved of their opinions <\s>
<s> bungay's opinions in truth were pretty simple <\s>
<s> he thought the captain could write the best smashing article in england <\s>
<s> he wanted the opposition house of bacon smashed and it was his opinion that the captain could do that business <\s>
<s> if the captain had written a letter of junius on a sheet of paper or copied a part of the church catechism mr <\s>
<s> bungay would have been perfectly contented and have considered that the article was a smashing article <\s>
<s> and he pocketed the papers with the greatest satisfaction and he not only paid for the ms as we have seen but he called little mary to him and gave her a penny as he went away <\s>
<s> the reading of the manuscript over the party engaged in general conversation shandon leading with a jaunty fashionable air in compliment to the two guests who sate with him and and who by their appearance and manner he presumed to be persons of the beau monde <\s>
<s> he knew very little indeed of the great world but he had seen it and made the most of what he had seen <\s>
<s> he spoke of the characters of the day and great personages of the fashion with easy familiarity and jocular allusions as if it had been his habit to live amongst them <\s>
<s> he told anecdotes of their private life and of conversations he had had and entertainments at which he had been present and at which such and such a thing occurred <\s>
<s> pen was amused to hear the shabby prisoner in a tattered dressing gown talking glibly about the great of the land <\s>
<s> shandon was always delighted when her husband told these tales and believed in them fondly every one <\s>
<s> she did not want to mingle in the fashionable world herself she was not clever enough but the great society was the very place for her charles he shone in it he was respected in it <\s>
<s> indeed shandon had once been asked to dinner by the earl of x his wife treasured the invitation card in her workbox at that very day <\s>
<s> bungay presently had enough of this talk and got up to take leave whereupon warrington and pen rose to depart with the publisher though the latter would have liked to stay to make a further acquaintance with this family who interested him and touched him <\s>
<s> he said something about hoping for permission to repeat his visit upon which shandon with a rueful grin said he was always to be found at home and should be delighted to see mr <\s>

<s> shandon sadly went on with her work at the window looking into the court <\s>
<s> she saw shandon with a couple of men at his heels run rapidly in the direction of the prison tavern <\s>
<s> she had hoped to have had him to dinner herself that day there was a piece of meat and some salad in a basin on the ledge outside of the window of their room which she had expected that she and little mary were to share with the child's father <\s>
<s> but there was no chance of that now <\s>
<s> he would be in that tavern until the hours for closing it then he would go and play at cards or drink in some other man's room and come back silent with glazed eyes reeling a little on his walk that his wife might nurse him <\s>

<s> jack finucane a townsman of captain shandon's found the captain's wife and little mary for whom jack always brought a sweetmeat in his pocket over this meal <\s>
<s> jack thought shandon the greatest of created geniuses had had one or two helps from the good natured prodigal who had always a kind word and sometimes a guinea for any friend in need and never missed a day in seeing his patron <\s>
<s> he was ready to run shandon's errands and transact his money business with publishers and newspaper editors duns creditors holders of shandon's acceptances gentlemen disposed to speculate in those securities and to transact the thousand little affairs of an embarrassed irish gentleman <\s>
<s> i never knew an embarrassed irish gentleman yet but he had an aide de camp of his own nation likewise in circumstances of pecuniary discomfort <\s>
<s> that aide de camp has subordinates of his own who again may have other insolvent dependents all through his life our captain marched at the head of a ragged staff who shared in the rough fortunes of their chieftain <\s>

<s> shandon had given a pound to one follower had sent a leg of mutton and potatoes and beer to an acquaintance in the poor side of the prison had paid an outstanding bill at the tavern where he had changed his five pound note had had a dinner with two friends there to whom he lost sundry half crowns at cards afterwards so that the night left him as poor as the morning had found him <\s>
<s> the publisher and the two gentlemen had had some talk together after quitting shandon and warrington reiterated to bungay what he had said to his rival bacon viz that pen was a high fellow of great genius and what was more well with the great world and related to no end of the peerage <\s>
<s> bungay replied that he should be happy to have dealings with mr <\s>

<s> we number influential friends in both houses of the senate and have secured allies in every diplomatic circle in europe <\s>
<s> our sources of intelligence are such as cannot by any possibility be made public and indeed such as no other london or european journal could by any chance acquire <\s>
<s> but this we are free to say that the very earliest information connected with the movement of english and continental politics will be found only in the columns of the pall mall gazette the statesman and the capitalist the country gentleman and the divine will be amongst our readers because our writers are amongst them <\s>
<s> we address ourselves to the higher circles of society we care not to disown it the pall mall gazette is written by gentlemen for gentlemen its conductors speak to the classes in which they live and were born <\s>
<s> the field preacher has his journal the radical free thinker has his journal why should the gentlemen of england be unrepresented in the press mr <\s>
<s> shandon then went on with much modesty to descant upon the literary and fashionable departments of the pall mall gazette which were to be conducted by gentlemen of acknowledged reputation men famous at the universities at which mr pendennis could scarcely help laughing and blushing known at the clubs and of the society which they described <\s>
<s> he pointed out delicately to advertisers that there would be no such medium as the pall mall gazette for giving publicity to their sales and he eloquently called upon the nobility of england the baronetage of england the revered clergy of england the bar of england the matrons the daughters the homes and hearths of england to rally round the good old cause and bungay at the conclusion of the reading woke up from a second snooze in which he had indulged himself and again said it was all right <\s>
<s> the reading of the prospectus concluded the gentlemen present entered into some details regarding the political and literary management of the paper and mr <\s>
<s> bungay sate by listening and nodding his head as if he understood what was the subject of their conversation and approved of their opinions <\s>
<s> bungay's opinions in truth were pretty simple <\s>
<s> he thought the captain could write the best smashing article in england <\s>
<s> he wanted the opposition house of bacon smashed and it was his opinion that the captain could do that business <\s>
<s> if the captain had written a letter of junius on a sheet of paper or copied a part of the church catechism mr <\s>
<s> bungay would have been perfectly contented and have considered that the article was a smashing article <\s>
<s> and he pocketed the papers with the greatest satisfaction and he not only paid for the ms as we have seen but he called little mary to him and gave her a penny as he went away <\s>
<s> the reading of the manuscript over the party engaged in general conversation shandon leading with a jaunty fashionable air in compliment to the two guests who sate with him and and who by their appearance and manner he presumed to be persons of the beau monde <\s>
<s> he knew very little indeed of the great world but he had seen it and made the most of what he had seen <\s>
<s> he spoke of the characters of the day and great personages of the fashion with easy familiarity and jocular allusions as if it had been his habit to live amongst them <\s>
<s> he told anecdotes of their private life and of conversations he had had and entertainments at which he had been present and at which such and such a thing occurred <\s>
<s> pen was amused to hear the shabby prisoner in a tattered dressing gown talking glibly about the great of the land <\s>
<s> shandon was always delighted when her husband told these tales and believed in them fondly every one <\s>
<s> she did not want to mingle in the fashionable world herself she was not clever enough but the great society was the very place for her charles he shone in it he was respected in it <\s>
<s> indeed shandon had once been asked to dinner by the earl of x his wife treasured the invitation card in her workbox at that very day <\s>
<s> bungay presently had enough of this talk and got up to take leave whereupon warrington and pen rose to depart with the publisher though the latter would have liked to stay to make a further acquaintance with this family who interested him and touched him <\s>
<s> he said something about hoping for permission to repeat his visit upon which shandon with a rueful grin said he was always to be found at home and should be delighted to see mr <\s>
<s> i'll see you to my park gate gentlemen said captain shandon seizing his hat in spite of a deprecatory look and a faint cry of charles from mrs <\s>
<s> and the captain in shabby slippers shuffled out before his guests leading the way through the dismal passages of the prison <\s>
<s> his hand was already fiddling with his waistcoat pocket where bungay's five pound note was as he took leave of the three gentlemen at the wicket one of them mr <\s>
<s> arthur pendennis being greatly relieved when he was out of the horrid place and again freely treading the flags of farringdon street <\s>
<s> shandon sadly went on with her work at the window looking into the court <\s>
<s> she saw shandon with a couple of men at his heels run rapidly in the direction of the prison tavern <\s>
<s> she had hoped to have had him to dinner herself that day there was a piece of meat and some salad in a basin on the ledge outside of the window of their room which she had expected that she and little mary were to share with the child's father <\s>
<s> but there was no chance of that now <\s>
<s> he would be in that tavern until the hours for closing it then he would go and play at cards or drink in some other man's room and come back silent with glazed eyes reeling a little on his walk that his wife might nurse him <\s>
<s> oh what varieties of pain do we not make our women suffer <\s>
<s> shandon went to the cupboard and in lieu of a dinner made herself some tea <\s>
<s> and in those varieties of pain of which we spoke anon what a part of confidante has that poor tea pot played ever since the kindly plant was introduced among us <\s>
<s> what myriads of women have cried over it to be sure <\s>
<s> what sick beds it has smoked by <\s>
<s> what fevered lips have received refreshment from out of it <\s>

<s> melissa and sacharissa are talking love secrets over it <\s>
<s> poor polly has it and her lover's letters upon the table his letters who was her lover yesterday and when it was with pleasure not despair she wept over them <\s>
<s> mary tripping noiselessly comes into her mother's bedroom bearing a cup of the consoler to the widow who will take no other food ruth is busy concocting it for her husband who is coming home from the harvest field one could fill a page with hints for such pictures finally mrs <\s>
<s> shandon and little mary sit down and drink their tea together while the captain goes out and takes his pleasure <\s>
<s> she cares for nothing else but that when her husband is away <\s>
<s> a gentleman with whom we are already slightly acquainted mr <\s>
<s> jack finucane a townsman of captain shandon's found the captain's wife and little mary for whom jack always brought a sweetmeat in his pocket over this meal <\s>
<s> jack thought shandon the greatest of created geniuses had had one or two helps from the good natured prodigal who had always a kind word and sometimes a guinea for any friend in need and never missed a day in seeing his patron <\s>
<s> he was ready to run shandon's errands and transact his money business with publishers and newspaper editors duns creditors holders of shandon's acceptances gentlemen disposed to speculate in those securities and to transact the thousand little affairs of an embarrassed irish gentleman <\s>
<s> i never knew an embarrassed irish gentleman yet but he had an aide de camp of his own nation likewise in circumstances of pecuniary discomfort <\s>
<s> that aide de camp has subordinates of his own who again may have other insolvent dependents all through his life our captain marched at the head of a ragged staff who shared in the rough fortunes of their chieftain <\s>
<s> he won't have that five pound note very long i bet a guinea mr <\s>
<s> bungay said of the captain as he and his two companions walked away from the prison and the publisher judged rightly for when mrs <\s>
<s> shandon came to empty her husband's pockets she found but a couple of shillings and a few halfpence out of the morning's remittance <\s>
<s> shandon had given a pound to one follower had sent a leg of mutton and potatoes and beer to an acquaintance in the poor side of the prison had paid an outstanding bill at the tavern where he had changed his five pound note had had a dinner with two friends there to whom he lost sundry half crowns at cards afterwards so that the night left him as poor as the morning had found him <\s>
<s> the publisher and the two gentlemen had had some talk together after quitting shandon and warrington reiterated to bungay what he had said to his rival bacon viz that pen was a high fellow of great genius and what was more well with the great world and related to no end of the peerage <\s>
<s> bungay replied that he should be happy to have dealings with mr <\s>
<s> pendennis and hoped to have the pleasure of seeing both gents to cut mutton with him before long and so with mutual politeness and protestations they parted <\s>
<s> it is hard to see such a man as shandon pen said musing and talking that night over the sight which he had witnessed of accomplishments so multifarious and of such an undoubted talent and humour an inmate of a gaol for half his time and a bookseller's hanger on when out of prison <\s>
<s> i am a bookseller's hanger on you are going to try your paces as a hack warrington said with a laugh <\s>
<s> we are all hacks upon some road or other <\s>
<s> i would rather be myself than paley our neighbour in chambers who has as much enjoyment of his life as a mole <\s>
<s> a deuced deal of undeserved compassion has been thrown away upon what you call your bookseller's drudge <\s>
<s> much solitary pipes and ale make a cynic of you said pen you are a diogenes by a beer barrel warrington <\s>

<s> bungay whom we have just left who fattens on the profits of the other's brains and enriches himself out of his journeyman's labour <\s>

<s> the captain then went on to confess with much candour that up to the present time the gentlemen of england confident of their right and careless of those who questioned it had left the political interest of their order as they did the management of their estates or the settlement of their legal affairs to persons affected to each peculiar service and had permitted their interests to be represented in the press by professional proctors and advocates <\s>
<s> that time shandon professed to consider was now gone by the gentlemen of england must be their own champions the declared enemies of their order were brave strong numerous and uncompromising <\s>

<s> he pointed out delicately to advertisers that there would be no such medium as the pall mall gazette for giving publicity to their sales and he eloquently called upon the nobility of england the baronetage of england the revered clergy of england the bar of england the matrons the daughters the homes and hearths of england to rally round the good old cause and bungay at the conclusion of the reading woke up from a second snooze in which he had indulged himself and again said it was all right <\s>
<s> the reading of the prospectus concluded the gentlemen present entered into some details regarding the political and literary management of the paper and mr <\s>
<s> bungay sate by listening and nodding his head as if he understood what was the subject of their conversation and approved of their opinions <\s>
<s> bungay's opinions in truth were pretty simple <\s>
<s> he thought the captain could write the best smashing article in england <\s>
<s> he wanted the opposition house of bacon smashed and it was his opinion that the captain could do that business <\s>
<s> if the captain had written a letter of junius on a sheet of paper or copied a part of the church catechism mr <\s>
<s> bungay would have been perfectly contented and have considered that the article was a smashing article <\s>
<s> and he pocketed the papers with the greatest satisfaction and he not only paid for the ms as we have seen but he called little mary to him and gave her a penny as he went away <\s>
<s> the reading of the manuscript over the party engaged in general conversation shandon leading with a jaunty fashionable air in compliment to the two guests who sate with him and and who by their appearance and manner he presumed to be persons of the beau monde <\s>
<s> he knew very little indeed of the great world but he had seen it and made the most of what he had seen <\s>
<s> he spoke of the characters of the day and great personages of the fashion with easy familiarity and jocular allusions as if it had been his habit to live amongst them <\s>
<s> he told anecdotes of their private life and of conversations he had had and entertainments at which he had been present and at which such and such a thing occurred <\s>

<s> shandon was always delighted when her husband told these tales and believed in them fondly every one <\s>
<s> she did not want to mingle in the fashionable world herself she was not clever enough but the great society was the very place for her charles he shone in it he was respected in it <\s>
<s> indeed shandon had once been asked to dinner by the earl of x his wife treasured the invitation card in her workbox at that very day <\s>
<s> bungay presently had enough of this talk and got up to take leave whereupon warrington and pen rose to depart with the publisher though the latter would have liked to stay to make a further acquaintance with this family who interested him and touched him <\s>
<s> he said something about hoping for permission to repeat his visit upon which shandon with a rueful grin said he was always to be found at home and should be delighted to see mr <\s>

<s> jack finucane a townsman of captain shandon's found the captain's wife and little mary for whom jack always brought a sweetmeat in his pocket over this meal <\s>
<s> jack thought shandon the greatest of created geniuses had had one or two helps from the good natured prodigal who had always a kind word and sometimes a guinea for any friend in need and never missed a day in seeing his patron <\s>
<s> he was ready to run shandon's errands and transact his money business with publishers and newspaper editors duns creditors holders of shandon's acceptances gentlemen disposed to speculate in those securities and to transact the thousand little affairs of an embarrassed irish gentleman <\s>
<s> i never knew an embarrassed irish gentleman yet but he had an aide de camp of his own nation likewise in circumstances of pecuniary discomfort <\s>
<s> that aide de camp has subordinates of his own who again may have other insolvent dependents all through his life our captain marched at the head of a ragged staff who shared in the rough fortunes of their chieftain <\s>

<s> bungay said of the captain as he and his two companions walked away from the prison and the publisher judged rightly for when mrs <\s>
<s> shandon came to empty her husband's pockets she found but a couple of shillings and a few halfpence out of the morning's remittance <\s>
<s> shandon had given a pound to one follower had sent a leg of mutton and potatoes and beer to an acquaintance in the poor side of the prison had paid an outstanding bill at the tavern where he had changed his five pound note had had a dinner with two friends there to whom he lost sundry half crowns at cards afterwards so that the night left him as poor as the morning had found him <\s>
<s> the publisher and the two gentlemen had had some talk together after quitting shandon and warrington reiterated to bungay what he had said to his rival bacon viz that pen was a high fellow of great genius and what was more well with the great world and related to no end of the peerage <\s>
<s> bungay replied that he should be happy to have dealings with mr <\s>
<s> pendennis and hoped to have the pleasure of seeing both gents to cut mutton with him before long and so with mutual politeness and protestations they parted <\s>
<s> it is hard to see such a man as shandon pen said musing and talking that night over the sight which he had witnessed of accomplishments so multifarious and of such an undoubted talent and humour an inmate of a gaol for half his time and a bookseller's hanger on when out of prison <\s>
<s> i am a bookseller's hanger on you are going to try your paces as a hack warrington said with a laugh <\s>
<s> we are all hacks upon some road or other <\s>
<s> i would rather be myself than paley our neighbour in chambers who has as much enjoyment of his life as a mole <\s>

<s> the captain then went on to confess with much candour that up to the present time the gentlemen of england confident of their right and careless of those who questioned it had left the political interest of their order as they did the management of their estates or the settlement of their legal affairs to persons affected to each peculiar service and had permitted their interests to be represented in the press by professional proctors and advocates <\s>
<s> that time shandon professed to consider was now gone by the gentlemen of england must be their own champions the declared enemies of their order were brave strong numerous and uncompromising <\s>

<s> he wanted the opposition house of bacon smashed and it was his opinion that the captain could do that business <\s>
<s> if the captain had written a letter of junius on a sheet of paper or copied a part of the church catechism mr <\s>
<s> bungay would have been perfectly contented and have considered that the article was a smashing article <\s>
<s> and he pocketed the papers with the greatest satisfaction and he not only paid for the ms as we have seen but he called little mary to him and gave her a penny as he went away <\s>
<s> the reading of the manuscript over the party engaged in general conversation shandon leading with a jaunty fashionable air in compliment to the two guests who sate with him and and who by their appearance and manner he presumed to be persons of the beau monde <\s>
<s> he knew very little indeed of the great world but he had seen it and made the most of what he had seen <\s>
<s> he spoke of the characters of the day and great personages of the fashion with easy familiarity and jocular allusions as if it had been his habit to live amongst them <\s>
<s> he told anecdotes of their private life and of conversations he had had and entertainments at which he had been present and at which such and such a thing occurred <\s>
<s> pen was amused to hear the shabby prisoner in a tattered dressing gown talking glibly about the great of the land <\s>
<s> shandon was always delighted when her husband told these tales and believed in them fondly every one <\s>
<s> she did not want to mingle in the fashionable world herself she was not clever enough but the great society was the very place for her charles he shone in it he was respected in it <\s>
<s> indeed shandon had once been asked to dinner by the earl of x his wife treasured the invitation card in her workbox at that very day <\s>
<s> bungay presently had enough of this talk and got up to take leave whereupon warrington and pen rose to depart with the publisher though the latter would have liked to stay to make a further acquaintance with this family who interested him and touched him <\s>
<s> he said something about hoping for permission to repeat his visit upon which shandon with a rueful grin said he was always to be found at home and should be delighted to see mr <\s>
<s> i'll see you to my park gate gentlemen said captain shandon seizing his hat in spite of a deprecatory look and a faint cry of charles from mrs <\s>
<s> and the captain in shabby slippers shuffled out before his guests leading the way through the dismal passages of the prison <\s>
<s> his hand was already fiddling with his waistcoat pocket where bungay's five pound note was as he took leave of the three gentlemen at the wicket one of them mr <\s>
<s> arthur pendennis being greatly relieved when he was out of the horrid place and again freely treading the flags of farringdon street <\s>
<s> shandon sadly went on with her work at the window looking into the court <\s>
<s> she saw shandon with a couple of men at his heels run rapidly in the direction of the prison tavern <\s>
<s> she had hoped to have had him to dinner herself that day there was a piece of meat and some salad in a basin on the ledge outside of the window of their room which she had expected that she and little mary were to share with the child's father <\s>
<s> but there was no chance of that now <\s>
<s> he would be in that tavern until the hours for closing it then he would go and play at cards or drink in some other man's room and come back silent with glazed eyes reeling a little on his walk that his wife might nurse him <\s>
<s> oh what varieties of pain do we not make our women suffer <\s>
<s> shandon went to the cupboard and in lieu of a dinner made herself some tea <\s>
<s> and in those varieties of pain of which we spoke anon what a part of confidante has that poor tea pot played ever since the kindly plant was introduced among us <\s>
<s> what myriads of women have cried over it to be sure <\s>
<s> what sick beds it has smoked by <\s>
<s> what fevered lips have received refreshment from out of it <\s>

<s> poor polly has it and her lover's letters upon the table his letters who was her lover yesterday and when it was with pleasure not despair she wept over them <\s>

<s> jack finucane a townsman of captain shandon's found the captain's wife and little mary for whom jack always brought a sweetmeat in his pocket over this meal <\s>
<s> jack thought shandon the greatest of created geniuses had had one or two helps from the good natured prodigal who had always a kind word and sometimes a guinea for any friend in need and never missed a day in seeing his patron <\s>
<s> he was ready to run shandon's errands and transact his money business with publishers and newspaper editors duns creditors holders of shandon's acceptances gentlemen disposed to speculate in those securities and to transact the thousand little affairs of an embarrassed irish gentleman <\s>
<s> i never knew an embarrassed irish gentleman yet but he had an aide de camp of his own nation likewise in circumstances of pecuniary discomfort <\s>
<s> that aide de camp has subordinates of his own who again may have other insolvent dependents all through his life our captain marched at the head of a ragged staff who shared in the rough fortunes of their chieftain <\s>
<s> he won't have that five pound note very long i bet a guinea mr <\s>
<s> bungay said of the captain as he and his two companions walked away from the prison and the publisher judged rightly for when mrs <\s>
<s> shandon came to empty her husband's pockets she found but a couple of shillings and a few halfpence out of the morning's remittance <\s>
<s> shandon had given a pound to one follower had sent a leg of mutton and potatoes and beer to an acquaintance in the poor side of the prison had paid an outstanding bill at the tavern where he had changed his five pound note had had a dinner with two friends there to whom he lost sundry half crowns at cards afterwards so that the night left him as poor as the morning had found him <\s>
<s> the publisher and the two gentlemen had had some talk together after quitting shandon and warrington reiterated to bungay what he had said to his rival bacon viz that pen was a high fellow of great genius and what was more well with the great world and related to no end of the peerage <\s>
<s> bungay replied that he should be happy to have dealings with mr <\s>
<s> pendennis and hoped to have the pleasure of seeing both gents to cut mutton with him before long and so with mutual politeness and protestations they parted <\s>
<s> it is hard to see such a man as shandon pen said musing and talking that night over the sight which he had witnessed of accomplishments so multifarious and of such an undoubted talent and humour an inmate of a gaol for half his time and a bookseller's hanger on when out of prison <\s>
<s> i am a bookseller's hanger on you are going to try your paces as a hack warrington said with a laugh <\s>
<s> we are all hacks upon some road or other <\s>
<s> i would rather be myself than paley our neighbour in chambers who has as much enjoyment of his life as a mole <\s>
<s> a deuced deal of undeserved compassion has been thrown away upon what you call your bookseller's drudge <\s>
<s> much solitary pipes and ale make a cynic of you said pen you are a diogenes by a beer barrel warrington <\s>
<s> no man shall tell me that a man of genius as shandon is ought to be driven by such a vulgar slave driver as yonder mr <\s>
<s> bungay whom we have just left who fattens on the profits of the other's brains and enriches himself out of his journeyman's labour <\s>
<s> it makes me indignant to see a gentleman the serf of such a creature as that of a man who can't speak the language that he lives by who is not fit to black shandon's boots <\s>
<s> so you have begun already to gird at the publishers and to take your side amongst our order <\s>
<s> bravo pen my be boy <\s>
<s> warrington answered laughing still <\s>
<s> what have you got to say against bungay's relations with shandon <\s>
<s> was it the publisher think you who sent the author to prison <\s>
<s> is it bungay who is tippling away the five pound note which we saw just now or shandon <\s>
<s> misfortune drives a man into bad company pen said <\s>
<s> it is easy to cry fie <\s>
<s> bungay nodded his head in a knowing manner and winked his eyes when the captain came to the waterloo passage and warrington burst out laughing <\s>
<s> you see how our venerable friend bungay is affected shandon said slily looking up from his papers that's your true sort of test <\s>
<s> i have used the duke of wellington and the battle of waterloo a hundred times and i never knew the duke to fail <\s>
<s> the captain then went on to confess with much candour that up to the present time the gentlemen of england confident of their right and careless of those who questioned it had left the political interest of their order as they did the management of their estates or the settlement of their legal affairs to persons affected to each peculiar service and had permitted their interests to be represented in the press by professional proctors and advocates <\s>
<s> that time shandon professed to consider was now gone by the gentlemen of england must be their own champions the declared enemies of their order were brave strong numerous and uncompromising <\s>
<s> they must meet their foes in the field they must not be belied and misrepresented by hireling advocates they must not have grub street publishing gazettes from whitehall that's a dig at bacon's people mr <\s>
<s> bungay said shandon turning round to the publisher <\s>
<s> bungay clapped his stick on the floor <\s>
<s> hang him pitch into him capting he said with exultation and turning to warrington wagged his dull head more vehemently than ever and said for a slashing article sir there's nobody like the capting no obody like him <\s>

<s> pen was amused to hear the shabby prisoner in a tattered dressing gown talking glibly about the great of the land <\s>
<s> shandon was always delighted when her husband told these tales and believed in them fondly every one <\s>
<s> she did not want to mingle in the fashionable world herself she was not clever enough but the great society was the very place for her charles he shone in it he was respected in it <\s>
<s> indeed shandon had once been asked to dinner by the earl of x his wife treasured the invitation card in her workbox at that very day <\s>
<s> bungay presently had enough of this talk and got up to take leave whereupon warrington and pen rose to depart with the publisher though the latter would have liked to stay to make a further acquaintance with this family who interested him and touched him <\s>
<s> he said something about hoping for permission to repeat his visit upon which shandon with a rueful grin said he was always to be found at home and should be delighted to see mr <\s>
<s> i'll see you to my park gate gentlemen said captain shandon seizing his hat in spite of a deprecatory look and a faint cry of charles from mrs <\s>
<s> and the captain in shabby slippers shuffled out before his guests leading the way through the dismal passages of the prison <\s>
<s> his hand was already fiddling with his waistcoat pocket where bungay's five pound note was as he took leave of the three gentlemen at the wicket one of them mr <\s>
<s> arthur pendennis being greatly relieved when he was out of the horrid place and again freely treading the flags of farringdon street <\s>
<s> shandon sadly went on with her work at the window looking into the court <\s>
<s> she saw shandon with a couple of men at his heels run rapidly in the direction of the prison tavern <\s>
<s> she had hoped to have had him to dinner herself that day there was a piece of meat and some salad in a basin on the ledge outside of the window of their room which she had expected that she and little mary were to share with the child's father <\s>
<s> but there was no chance of that now <\s>
<s> he would be in that tavern until the hours for closing it then he would go and play at cards or drink in some other man's room and come back silent with glazed eyes reeling a little on his walk that his wife might nurse him <\s>
<s> oh what varieties of pain do we not make our women suffer <\s>
<s> shandon went to the cupboard and in lieu of a dinner made herself some tea <\s>
<s> and in those varieties of pain of which we spoke anon what a part of confidante has that poor tea pot played ever since the kindly plant was introduced among us <\s>
<s> what myriads of women have cried over it to be sure <\s>
<s> what sick beds it has smoked by <\s>
<s> what fevered lips have received refreshment from out of it <\s>

<s> poor polly has it and her lover's letters upon the table his letters who was her lover yesterday and when it was with pleasure not despair she wept over them <\s>

<s> shandon and little mary sit down and drink their tea together while the captain goes out and takes his pleasure <\s>
<s> she cares for nothing else but that when her husband is away <\s>
<s> a gentleman with whom we are already slightly acquainted mr <\s>
<s> jack finucane a townsman of captain shandon's found the captain's wife and little mary for whom jack always brought a sweetmeat in his pocket over this meal <\s>
<s> jack thought shandon the greatest of created geniuses had had one or two helps from the good natured prodigal who had always a kind word and sometimes a guinea for any friend in need and never missed a day in seeing his patron <\s>
<s> he was ready to run shandon's errands and transact his money business with publishers and newspaper editors duns creditors holders of shandon's acceptances gentlemen disposed to speculate in those securities and to transact the thousand little affairs of an embarrassed irish gentleman <\s>
<s> i never knew an embarrassed irish gentleman yet but he had an aide de camp of his own nation likewise in circumstances of pecuniary discomfort <\s>
<s> that aide de camp has subordinates of his own who again may have other insolvent dependents all through his life our captain marched at the head of a ragged staff who shared in the rough fortunes of their chieftain <\s>
<s> he won't have that five pound note very long i bet a guinea mr <\s>
<s> bungay said of the captain as he and his two companions walked away from the prison and the publisher judged rightly for when mrs <\s>
<s> shandon came to empty her husband's pockets she found but a couple of shillings and a few halfpence out of the morning's remittance <\s>
<s> shandon had given a pound to one follower had sent a leg of mutton and potatoes and beer to an acquaintance in the poor side of the prison had paid an outstanding bill at the tavern where he had changed his five pound note had had a dinner with two friends there to whom he lost sundry half crowns at cards afterwards so that the night left him as poor as the morning had found him <\s>
<s> the publisher and the two gentlemen had had some talk together after quitting shandon and warrington reiterated to bungay what he had said to his rival bacon viz that pen was a high fellow of great genius and what was more well with the great world and related to no end of the peerage <\s>
<s> bungay replied that he should be happy to have dealings with mr <\s>
<s> pendennis and hoped to have the pleasure of seeing both gents to cut mutton with him before long and so with mutual politeness and protestations they parted <\s>
<s> it is hard to see such a man as shandon pen said musing and talking that night over the sight which he had witnessed of accomplishments so multifarious and of such an undoubted talent and humour an inmate of a gaol for half his time and a bookseller's hanger on when out of prison <\s>
<s> i am a bookseller's hanger on you are going to try your paces as a hack warrington said with a laugh <\s>
<s> we are all hacks upon some road or other <\s>
<s> i would rather be myself than paley our neighbour in chambers who has as much enjoyment of his life as a mole <\s>
<s> a deuced deal of undeserved compassion has been thrown away upon what you call your bookseller's drudge <\s>
<s> much solitary pipes and ale make a cynic of you said pen you are a diogenes by a beer barrel warrington <\s>
<s> no man shall tell me that a man of genius as shandon is ought to be driven by such a vulgar slave driver as yonder mr <\s>
<s> bungay whom we have just left who fattens on the profits of the other's brains and enriches himself out of his journeyman's labour <\s>
<s> it makes me indignant to see a gentleman the serf of such a creature as that of a man who can't speak the language that he lives by who is not fit to black shandon's boots <\s>
<s> so you have begun already to gird at the publishers and to take your side amongst our order <\s>
<s> bravo pen my be boy <\s>
<s> warrington answered laughing still <\s>
<s> what have you got to say against bungay's relations with shandon <\s>
<s> was it the publisher think you who sent the author to prison <\s>
<s> is it bungay who is tippling away the five pound note which we saw just now or shandon <\s>
<s> misfortune drives a man into bad company pen said <\s>
<s> it is easy to cry fie <\s>
<s> bungay nodded his head in a knowing manner and winked his eyes when the captain came to the waterloo passage and warrington burst out laughing <\s>
<s> you see how our venerable friend bungay is affected shandon said slily looking up from his papers that's your true sort of test <\s>
<s> i have used the duke of wellington and the battle of waterloo a hundred times and i never knew the duke to fail <\s>
<s> the captain then went on to confess with much candour that up to the present time the gentlemen of england confident of their right and careless of those who questioned it had left the political interest of their order as they did the management of their estates or the settlement of their legal affairs to persons affected to each peculiar service and had permitted their interests to be represented in the press by professional proctors and advocates <\s>
<s> that time shandon professed to consider was now gone by the gentlemen of england must be their own champions the declared enemies of their order were brave strong numerous and uncompromising <\s>
<s> they must meet their foes in the field they must not be belied and misrepresented by hireling advocates they must not have grub street publishing gazettes from whitehall that's a dig at bacon's people mr <\s>
<s> bungay said shandon turning round to the publisher <\s>
<s> bungay clapped his stick on the floor <\s>
<s> hang him pitch into him capting he said with exultation and turning to warrington wagged his dull head more vehemently than ever and said for a slashing article sir there's nobody like the capting no obody like him <\s>
<s> the prospectus writer went on to say that some gentlemen whose names were for obvious reasons not brought before the public at which mr <\s>
<s> warrington began to laugh again had determined to bring forward a journal of which the principles were so and so <\s>
<s> these men are proud of their order and anxious to uphold it cried out captain shandon flourishing his paper with a grin <\s>
<s> they are loyal to their sovereign by faithful conviction and ancestral allegiance they love their church where they would have their children worship and for which their forefathers bled they love their country and would keep it what the gentlemen of england yes the gentlemen of england we'll have that in large caps bungay my boy have made it the greatest and freest in the world and as the names of some of them are appended to the deed which secured our liberties at runnymede what's that <\s>
<s> an ancestor of mine sealed it with his sword hilt pen said with great gravity <\s>
<s> it's the habeas corpus mr <\s>
<s> bungay warrington said on which the publisher answered all right i dare say and yawned though he said go on capting <\s>
<s> at runnymede they are ready to defend that freedom to day with sword and pen and now as then to rally round the old laws and liberties of england <\s>
<s> the little child stood wondering the lady was working silently and looking with fond admiration <\s>
<s> come here little mary said warrington and patted the child's fair curls with his large hand <\s>
<s> but she shrank back from his rough caress and preferred to go and take refuge at pen's knee and play with his fine watch chain and pen was very much pleased that she came to him for he was very soft hearted and simple though he concealed his gentleness under a shy and pompous demeanour <\s>
<s> so she clambered up on his lap whilst her father continued to read his programme <\s>

<s> the field preacher has his journal the radical free thinker has his journal why should the gentlemen of england be unrepresented in the press mr <\s>
<s> shandon then went on with much modesty to descant upon the literary and fashionable departments of the pall mall gazette which were to be conducted by gentlemen of acknowledged reputation men famous at the universities at which mr pendennis could scarcely help laughing and blushing known at the clubs and of the society which they described <\s>
<s> he pointed out delicately to advertisers that there would be no such medium as the pall mall gazette for giving publicity to their sales and he eloquently called upon the nobility of england the baronetage of england the revered clergy of england the bar of england the matrons the daughters the homes and hearths of england to rally round the good old cause and bungay at the conclusion of the reading woke up from a second snooze in which he had indulged himself and again said it was all right <\s>

<s> i'll see you to my park gate gentlemen said captain shandon seizing his hat in spite of a deprecatory look and a faint cry of charles from mrs <\s>
<s> and the captain in shabby slippers shuffled out before his guests leading the way through the dismal passages of the prison <\s>

<s> arthur pendennis being greatly relieved when he was out of the horrid place and again freely treading the flags of farringdon street <\s>
<s> shandon sadly went on with her work at the window looking into the court <\s>
<s> she saw shandon with a couple of men at his heels run rapidly in the direction of the prison tavern <\s>
<s> she had hoped to have had him to dinner herself that day there was a piece of meat and some salad in a basin on the ledge outside of the window of their room which she had expected that she and little mary were to share with the child's father <\s>
<s> but there was no chance of that now <\s>
<s> he would be in that tavern until the hours for closing it then he would go and play at cards or drink in some other man's room and come back silent with glazed eyes reeling a little on his walk that his wife might nurse him <\s>
<s> oh what varieties of pain do we not make our women suffer <\s>
<s> shandon went to the cupboard and in lieu of a dinner made herself some tea <\s>

<s> what sick beds it has smoked by <\s>
<s> what fevered lips have received refreshment from out of it <\s>

<s> jack finucane a townsman of captain shandon's found the captain's wife and little mary for whom jack always brought a sweetmeat in his pocket over this meal <\s>
<s> jack thought shandon the greatest of created geniuses had had one or two helps from the good natured prodigal who had always a kind word and sometimes a guinea for any friend in need and never missed a day in seeing his patron <\s>
<s> he was ready to run shandon's errands and transact his money business with publishers and newspaper editors duns creditors holders of shandon's acceptances gentlemen disposed to speculate in those securities and to transact the thousand little affairs of an embarrassed irish gentleman <\s>
<s> i never knew an embarrassed irish gentleman yet but he had an aide de camp of his own nation likewise in circumstances of pecuniary discomfort <\s>
<s> that aide de camp has subordinates of his own who again may have other insolvent dependents all through his life our captain marched at the head of a ragged staff who shared in the rough fortunes of their chieftain <\s>
<s> he won't have that five pound note very long i bet a guinea mr <\s>
<s> bungay said of the captain as he and his two companions walked away from the prison and the publisher judged rightly for when mrs <\s>
<s> shandon came to empty her husband's pockets she found but a couple of shillings and a few halfpence out of the morning's remittance <\s>
<s> shandon had given a pound to one follower had sent a leg of mutton and potatoes and beer to an acquaintance in the poor side of the prison had paid an outstanding bill at the tavern where he had changed his five pound note had had a dinner with two friends there to whom he lost sundry half crowns at cards afterwards so that the night left him as poor as the morning had found him <\s>
<s> the publisher and the two gentlemen had had some talk together after quitting shandon and warrington reiterated to bungay what he had said to his rival bacon viz that pen was a high fellow of great genius and what was more well with the great world and related to no end of the peerage <\s>
<s> bungay replied that he should be happy to have dealings with mr <\s>
<s> pendennis and hoped to have the pleasure of seeing both gents to cut mutton with him before long and so with mutual politeness and protestations they parted <\s>
<s> it is hard to see such a man as shandon pen said musing and talking that night over the sight which he had witnessed of accomplishments so multifarious and of such an undoubted talent and humour an inmate of a gaol for half his time and a bookseller's hanger on when out of prison <\s>
<s> i am a bookseller's hanger on you are going to try your paces as a hack warrington said with a laugh <\s>
<s> we are all hacks upon some road or other <\s>
<s> i would rather be myself than paley our neighbour in chambers who has as much enjoyment of his life as a mole <\s>
<s> a deuced deal of undeserved compassion has been thrown away upon what you call your bookseller's drudge <\s>
<s> much solitary pipes and ale make a cynic of you said pen you are a diogenes by a beer barrel warrington <\s>
<s> no man shall tell me that a man of genius as shandon is ought to be driven by such a vulgar slave driver as yonder mr <\s>
<s> bungay whom we have just left who fattens on the profits of the other's brains and enriches himself out of his journeyman's labour <\s>
<s> it makes me indignant to see a gentleman the serf of such a creature as that of a man who can't speak the language that he lives by who is not fit to black shandon's boots <\s>
<s> so you have begun already to gird at the publishers and to take your side amongst our order <\s>
<s> bravo pen my be boy <\s>
<s> warrington answered laughing still <\s>
<s> what have you got to say against bungay's relations with shandon <\s>
<s> was it the publisher think you who sent the author to prison <\s>
<s> is it bungay who is tippling away the five pound note which we saw just now or shandon <\s>
<s> misfortune drives a man into bad company pen said <\s>
<s> it is easy to cry fie <\s>
<s> bungay nodded his head in a knowing manner and winked his eyes when the captain came to the waterloo passage and warrington burst out laughing <\s>
<s> you see how our venerable friend bungay is affected shandon said slily looking up from his papers that's your true sort of test <\s>
<s> i have used the duke of wellington and the battle of waterloo a hundred times and i never knew the duke to fail <\s>
<s> the captain then went on to confess with much candour that up to the present time the gentlemen of england confident of their right and careless of those who questioned it had left the political interest of their order as they did the management of their estates or the settlement of their legal affairs to persons affected to each peculiar service and had permitted their interests to be represented in the press by professional proctors and advocates <\s>
<s> that time shandon professed to consider was now gone by the gentlemen of england must be their own champions the declared enemies of their order were brave strong numerous and uncompromising <\s>
<s> they must meet their foes in the field they must not be belied and misrepresented by hireling advocates they must not have grub street publishing gazettes from whitehall that's a dig at bacon's people mr <\s>
<s> bungay said shandon turning round to the publisher <\s>
<s> bungay clapped his stick on the floor <\s>
<s> hang him pitch into him capting he said with exultation and turning to warrington wagged his dull head more vehemently than ever and said for a slashing article sir there's nobody like the capting no obody like him <\s>
<s> the prospectus writer went on to say that some gentlemen whose names were for obvious reasons not brought before the public at which mr <\s>
<s> warrington began to laugh again had determined to bring forward a journal of which the principles were so and so <\s>
<s> these men are proud of their order and anxious to uphold it cried out captain shandon flourishing his paper with a grin <\s>
<s> they are loyal to their sovereign by faithful conviction and ancestral allegiance they love their church where they would have their children worship and for which their forefathers bled they love their country and would keep it what the gentlemen of england yes the gentlemen of england we'll have that in large caps bungay my boy have made it the greatest and freest in the world and as the names of some of them are appended to the deed which secured our liberties at runnymede what's that <\s>
<s> an ancestor of mine sealed it with his sword hilt pen said with great gravity <\s>
<s> it's the habeas corpus mr <\s>
<s> bungay warrington said on which the publisher answered all right i dare say and yawned though he said go on capting <\s>
<s> at runnymede they are ready to defend that freedom to day with sword and pen and now as then to rally round the old laws and liberties of england <\s>
<s> the little child stood wondering the lady was working silently and looking with fond admiration <\s>
<s> come here little mary said warrington and patted the child's fair curls with his large hand <\s>
<s> but she shrank back from his rough caress and preferred to go and take refuge at pen's knee and play with his fine watch chain and pen was very much pleased that she came to him for he was very soft hearted and simple though he concealed his gentleness under a shy and pompous demeanour <\s>
<s> so she clambered up on his lap whilst her father continued to read his programme <\s>

<s> shandon then went on with much modesty to descant upon the literary and fashionable departments of the pall mall gazette which were to be conducted by gentlemen of acknowledged reputation men famous at the universities at which mr pendennis could scarcely help laughing and blushing known at the clubs and of the society which they described <\s>
<s> he pointed out delicately to advertisers that there would be no such medium as the pall mall gazette for giving publicity to their sales and he eloquently called upon the nobility of england the baronetage of england the revered clergy of england the bar of england the matrons the daughters the homes and hearths of england to rally round the good old cause and bungay at the conclusion of the reading woke up from a second snooze in which he had indulged himself and again said it was all right <\s>
